\n294\t    echo -e \"${YELLOW}$prompt${NC} \"\n295\t    read -r response\n296\t    \n297\t    case \"$response\" in\n298\t        [yY]|[yY][eE][sS])\n299\t            return 0\n300\t            ;;\n301\t        [nN]|[nN][oO])\n302\t            return 1\n303\t            ;;\n304\t        \"\")\n305\t            [[ \"$default\" == \"y\" ]] && return 0 || return 1\n306\t            ;;\n307\t        *)\n308\t            print_warning \"Please answer yes or no.\"\n309\t            confirm \"$1\" \"$default\"\n310\t            ;;\n311\t    esac\n312\t}\n313\t\n314\t# Prompt for input with validation\n315\tprompt_input() {\n316\t    local prompt=\"$1\"\n317\t    local validator=\"$2\"  # Optional validation function\n318\t    local default=\"$3\"    # Optional default value\n319\t    \n320\t    while true; do\n321\t        echo -e \"${BLUE}$prompt${NC}\"\n322\t        if [[ -n \"$default\" ]]; then\n323\t            echo -e \"${DIM}(default: $default)${NC}\"\n324\t        fi\n325\t        echo -n \"> \"\n326\t        read -r input\n327\t        \n328\t        # Use default if no input provided\n329\t        if [[ -z \"$input\" && -n \"$default\" ]]; then\n330\t            input=\"$default\"\n331\t        fi\n332\t        \n333\t        # Validate input if validator function provided\n334\t        if [[ -n \"$validator\" ]]; then\n335\t            if \"$validator\" Please try again.\"\n340\t                continue\n341\t            fi\n342\t        else\n343\t            echo \"$input\"\n344\t            return 0\n345\t        fi\n346\t    done\n347\t}\n348\t\n349\t# =============================================================================\n350\t# String Manipulation Functions\n351\t# =============================================================================\n352\t\n353\t# Convert string to lowercase\n354\tto_lower() {\n355\t    echo \"$1\" | tr '[:upper:]' '[:lower:]'\n356\t}\n357\t\n358\t# Convert string to uppercase\n359\tto_upper() {\n360\t    echo \"$1\" | tr '[:lower:]' '[:upper:]'\n361\t}\n362\t\n363\t# Trim whitespace from string\n364\ttrim() {\n365\t    local str=\"$1\"\n366\t    str=\"${str#\"${str%%[![:space:]]*}\"}\"  # Remove leading whitespace\n367\t    str=\"${str%\"${str##*[![:space:]]}\"}\"  # Remove trailing whitespace\n368\t printf \"%-*s\" \"$length\" \"$str\" | tr ' ' \"$char\"\n378\t}\n379\t\n380\t# =============================================================================\n381\t# Array Functions\n382\t# =============================================================================\n383\t\n384\t# Check if array contains element\n385\tarray_contains() {\n386\t    local element=\"$1\"\n387\t    shift\n388\t    local array=(\"$@\")\n389\t    \n390\t    for item in \"${array[@]}\"; do\n391\t        [[ \"$item\" == \"$element\" ]] && return 0\n392\t    done\n393\t    return 1\n394\t}\n395\t\n396\t# Join array elements with delimiter\n397\tarray_join() {\n398\t    local delimiter=\"$1\"\n399\t    shift\n400\t    local array=(\"$@\")\n401\t    \n402\t    local result=\"\"\n403\t    for item in \"${array[@]}\"; do\n404\t        if [[ -z \"$result\" ]]; then\n405\t            result=\"$item\"\n406\t        else\n407\t            result=\"$result$delimiter$item\"\n408\t        fi\n409\t    done\n410\t    echo \"$result\"\n411\t}\n412\t\n413\t#   echo \"$(get_supermac_dir)/config\"\n426\t}\n427\t\n428\t# Load configuration value\n429\tget_config() {\n430\t    local key=\"$1\"\n431\t    local default=\"$2\"\n432\t    local config_file=\"$(get_config_dir)/config.json\"\n433\t    \n434\t    if file_exists \"$config_file\" && command_exists jq; then\n435\t        local value\n436\t        value=$(jq -r \".$key // ((frame++))\n481\t    done\n482\t}\n483\t\n484\t# =============================================================================\n485\t# Performance Functions\n486\t# +%s.%N)\n492\t    \n493\t    \"$@\"\n494\t    local exit_code=$?\n495\t    \n496\t    local end_time\n497\t    end_time=$(date +%s.%N)\n498\t    local duration\n499\t    duration=$(echo \"$end_time -      - Show WiFi connection status\n13\t#   scan           - Scan for available networks\n14\t#   connect <name> - Connect to network\n15\t#   forget <name>  - Forget saved network\n16\t#   info           - Detailed connection information\n17\t#\n18\t# Built by CosmoLabs - https://cosmolabs.org\n19\t# =============================================================================\n20\t\n21\t# =============================================================================\n22\t# WiFi Power Management\n23\t# =============================================================================\n24\t\n25\twifi_get_interface() {\n26\t    # Get the WiFi interface name (usually en0 or en1)\n27\t    networksetup   if [[ -z \"$interface\" ]]; then\n35\t        echo \"unknown\"\n36\t        return 1\n37\t    fi\n38\t    \n39\t    local state\n40\t    state=$(networksetup -getairportpower \"$interface\" 1\n69\t        if [[ \"$(wifi_get_power_state)\" == \"On\" ]]; then\n70\t            break\n71\t        fi\n72\t        ((count++))\n73\t    done\n74\t    \n75\t    if [[ \"$(wifi_get_power_state)\"   else\n81\t        print_error \"Failed to turn WiFi on\"\n82\t        return 1\n83\t    fi\n84\t}\n85\t\n86\twifi_off() {\n87\t    local interface\n88\t    interface=$(wifi_get_interface)\n89\t    \n90\t    if [[ -z \"$interface\" ]]; then\n91\t        print_error \"WiFi interface not found\"\n92\t        return 1\n93\t    fi\n94\t    \n95\t    local current_state\n96\t \n122\t    print_info \"Current WiFi state: $current_state\"\n123\t    \n124\t    case \"$current_state\" in\n125\t        \"On\")\n126\t            wifi_off\n127\t            ;;\n128\t        \"Off\")\n129\t            wifi_on\n130\t            ;;\n131\t        *)\n132\t            print_error \"Unable to determine WiFi state\"\n133\t            return 1\n134\t            ;;\n135\t    esac\n136\t}\n137\t\n138\t# =============================================================================\n139\t# WiFi Network Information\n140\t# \n146\t    if [[ -z \"$interface\" ]]; then\n147\t        return 1\n148\t    fi\n149\t    \n150\t    local network\n151\t    network=$(networksetup -getairportnetwork \"$interface\" 2>/dev/null | sed =============================================================================\n267\t# Network Scanning and Management\n268\t# =============================================================================\n269\t\n270\twifi_scan() {\n271\t    local interface\n272\t    interface=$(wifi_get_interface)\n273\t    \n274\t    if [[ \n466\t    case \"$action\" in\n467\t        \"on\"|\"enable\")\n468\t            wifi_on\n469\t            ;;\n470\t        \"off\"|\"disable\")\n471\t            wifi_off\n472\t            ;;\n473\t $(basename \"$app_path\" .app) to dock...\"\n360\t    \n361\t    # Add to dock using dockutil if available, otherwise use defaults\n362\t    if command_exists dockutil; then\n363\t        if dockutil $app_path\"\n372\t        print_info \"You can manually drag the app to your dock\"\n373\t    fi\n374\t}\n375\t\n376\tdock_remove_app() {\n377\t    local app_name=\"$1\"\n378\t    \n379\t    if [[ -z \n535\t    case \"$action\" in\n536\t        \"position\")\n537\t            dock_set_position \"$1\"\n538\t            ;;\n539\t        \"autohide\")\n540\t            dock_set_autohide \"$1\"\n541\t \n121\t    local location_info\n122\t    location_info=$(curl -s --connect-timeout 5 \"https://ipinfo.io/$ip/json\" 2>/dev/null)\n123\t    \n124\t    if [[ -n \"$location_info\" ]]; then\n125\t =============================================================================\n281\t# Network Management\n282\t# =============================================================================\n283\t\n284\tnetwork_renew_dhcp() {\n285\t    local interface\n286\t    interface=$(network_get_interface_for_ip)\n287\t    \n288\t    if [[ -z \"$interface\" ]]; then\n289\t        print_error \"No active network interface found\"\n290\t        return 1\n291\t    fi\n292\t    \n293\t    print_info \"Renewing DHCP lease =============================================================================\n318\t# Developer Utilities\n319\t# =============================================================================\n106\t# System Cleanup Functions\n107\t# =============================================================================\n108\t\n109\tsystem_cleanup() {\n110\t    print_header \"🧹 System Cleanup\"\n111\t    echo \"\"\n112\t    \n113\t    print_warning \"This will clean caches, logs, and temporary files\"\n114\t    if ! confirm \"Continue with system cleanup?\" \"y\"; then\n115\t        print_info \"Cleanup cancelled\"\n116\t        return 0\n117\t    fi\n118\t    \n119\t    echo \"\"\n120\t    local cleaned_size=0\n121\t    \n122\t    # User caches\n123\t    if [[ -d \"$HOME/Library/Caches\" ]]; then\n124\t        print_info \"Cleaning user caches...\"\n125\t        local cache_size\n126\t        cache_size=$(du -sk \"$HOME/Library/Caches\" 2>/dev/null | awk '{print $1}')\n127\t        \n128\t        find \"$HOME/Library/Caches\" -type f -atime +7 -delete 2>/dev/null || true\n129\t        find \"$HOME/Library/Caches\" -type d -empty -delete 2>/dev/null || true\n130\t        \n131\t        cleaned_size=$((cleaned_size + cache_size))\n132\t        print_success \"User caches cleaned\"\n133\t    fi\n134\t    \n135\t    # Downloads cleanup (files older than 30 days)\n136\t    if [[ -d \"$HOME/Downloads\" ]]; then\n137\t        print_info \"Cleaning old downloads (30+ days)...\"\n138\t        local downloads_count\n139\t        downloads_count=$(find \"$HOME/Downloads\" -type f true\n143\t            print_success \"Cleaned $downloads_count old download files\"\n144\t        else\n145\t            print_info \"No old downloads to clean\"\n146\t        fi\n147\t    fi\n148\t    \n149\t    # Trash\n150\t    print_info \"Emptying trash...\"\n151\t    osascript -e 'tell application \"Finder\" to empty trash' 2>/dev/null || true\n152\t    print_success \"Trash emptied\"\n153\t required)...\"\n157\t        sudo find /var/log -name \"*.log\" -mtime +7 -delete 2>/dev/null || true\n158\t        sudo find /private/var/log -name \"*.log\" -mtime +7 -delete 2>/dev/null || restarting applications to free additional memory\"\n184\t    print_info \"💡 Use 'mac system memory' to check current memory usage\"\n185\t}\n186\t\n187\t# =============================================================================\n188\t# Battery Information\n189\t# =============================================================================\n190\t\n191\tsystem_battery() {\n192\t    # Check if this is a laptop\n193\t    if ! system_profiler SPPowerDataType >/dev/null 2>&1; then\n194\t        print_info \"No battery information available (desktop Mac)\"\n195\t        return 0\n196\t    fi\n197\t    \n198\t    print_header \"🔋 Battery Information\"\n199\t    echo \"\"\n200\t    \n201\t    # Get battery info using pmset\n202\t    local battery_info\n203\t    battery_info=$(pmset -g batt 2>/dev/null)\n204\t    \n205\t    if [[ -n \"$battery_info\" ]]; then\n206\t        # Parse battery percentage and status\n207\t        local percentage status time_remaining\n208\t        percentage=$(echo \"$battery_info\" | grep -E \"InternalBattery\" | awk '{print $3}' | sed 's/;//')\n209\t        status=$(echo \"$battery_info\" | grep -E \"InternalBattery\" | awk '{print $4}' | sed 's/;//')\n210\t        time_remaining=$(echo \"$battery_info\" | grep -E \"InternalBattery\" | awk '{for(i=5;i<=NF;i++) printf \"%s \", $i; print \"\"}' | trim)\n211\t        \n212\t        echo \"  Charge: $(print_command \"$percentage\")\"\n213\t        echo \"  Status: $(print_command \"$status\")\"\n214\t        \n215\t        if [[ -n \"$time_remaining\" && \"$time_remaining\" != \"(no estimate)\" ]]; then\n216\t            echo \"  Time remaining: $(print_command \"$time_remaining\")\"\n217\t        fi\n218\t    fi\n219\t    \n220\t    # Battery health information\n221\t    local cycle_count max_capacity\n222\t    cycle_count=$(system_profiler SPPowerDataType 2>/dev/null | grep \"Cycle Count\" | awk -F': ' '{print $2}' | trim)\n223\t    max_capacity=$(system_profiler SPPowerDataType 2>/dev/null | grep \"Maximum Capacity\" | awk -F': ' '{print $2}' | trim)\n224\t    \n225\t    if [[ -n \"$cycle_count\" ]]; then\n226\t        echo \"  Cycle count: $(print_command \"$cycle_count\")\"\n227\t    fi\n228\t    \n229\t    if [[ -n \"$max_capacity\" ]]; then\n230\t        echo \"  Maximum capacity: $(print_command \"$max_capacity\")\"\n231\t        \n232\t        # Health assessment\n233\t        local capacity_num\n234\t        capacity_num=$(echo \"$max_capacity\" | sed 's/%//')\n235\t        if [[ \"$capacity_num\" -gt 80 ]]; then\n236\t            print_success \"Battery health: Good\"\n237\t        elif [[ \"$capacity_num\" -gt 60 ]]; then\n238\t            print_warning \"Battery health: Fair\"\n239\t        else\n240\t            print_warning \"Battery health: Poor (consider replacement)\"\n241\t        fi\n242\t    fi\n243\t    \n244\t    # Power adapter status\n245\t    local adapter_info\n246\t    adapter_info=$(pmset -g ac 2>/dev/null)\n247\t    if [[ \"$adapter_info\" == *\"AC Power\"* ]]; then\n248\t        echo \"  Power adapter: $(print_command \"Connected\")\"\n249\t    else\n250\t        echo \"  Power adapter: $(print_dim \"Not connected\")\"\n251\t    fi\n252\t}\n253\t\n254\t# =============================================================================\n255\t# Memory Information\n256\t# =============================================================================\n257\t\n258\tsystem_memory() {\n259\t    print_header \"💾 Memory Usage\"\n260\t    echo \"\"\n261\t    \n262\t    # Get memory statistics\n263\t    local memory_info\n264\t    memory_info=$(vm_stat)\n265\t    \n266\t    local page_size=4096\n267\t    local pages_free pages_active pages_inactive pages_wired pages_compressed\n268\t    \n269\t    pages_free=$(echo \"$memory_info\" | grep \"Pages free\" | awk '{print $3}' | sed 's/\\.//')\n270\t    pages_active=$(echo \"$memory_info\" | grep \"Pages active\" | awk '{print $3}' | sed 's/\\.//')\n271\t    pages_inactive=$(echo \"$memory_info\" | grep \"Pages inactive\" | awk '{print $3}' | sed 's/\\.//')\n272\t    pages_wired=$(echo \"$memory_info\" | grep \"Pages wired down\" | awk '{print $4}' | sed 's/\\.//')\n273\t    pages_compressed=$(echo \"$memory_info\" | grep \"Pages stored in compressor\" | awk '{print $5}' | sed 's/\\.//' 2>/dev/null || echo \"0\")\n274\t    \n275\t    # Convert to MB\n276\t    local free_mb active_mb inactive_mb wired_mb compressed_mb total_mb used_mb\n277\t    free_mb=$((pages_free * page_size / 1024 / 1024))\n278\t    active_mb=$((pages_active * page_size / 1024 / 1024))\n279\t    inactive_mb=$((pages_inactive * page_size / 1024 / 1024))\n280\t    wired_mb=$((pages_wired * page_size / 1024 / 1024))\n281\t    compressed_mb=$((pages_compressed * page_size / 1024 / 1024))\n282\t    \n283\t    used_mb=$((active_mb + inactive_mb + wired_mb))\n284\t    total_mb=$((free_mb + used_mb))\n285\t    \n286\t    echo \"  Total: $(print_command \"${total_mb} MB\")\"\n287\t    echo \"  Used: $(print_command \"${used_mb} MB\")\"\n288\t    echo \"  Free: $(print_command \"${free_mb} MB\")\"\n289\t    echo \"\"\n290\t    echo \"  Active: $(print_command \"${active_mb} MB\")\"\n291\t    echo \"  Inactive: $(print_command \"${inactive_mb} MB\")\"\n292\t    echo \"  Wired: $(print_command \"${wired_mb} MB\")\"\n293\t    \n294\t    if [[ $compressed_mb -gt 0 ]]; then\n295\t        echo \"  Compressed: $(print_command \"${compressed_mb} MB\")\"\n296\t    fi\n297\t 's/%//')\n301\t    \n302\t    if [[ -n \"$memory_pressure\" ]]; then\n303\t        echo \"\"\n304\t        if [[ \"$memory_pressure\" -gt 20 ]]; then\n305\t            print_success \"Memory pressure: Low ($memory_pressure% free)\"\n306\t        elif [[ \"$memory_pressure\" -gt 10 ]]; then\n307\t            print_warning \"Memory pressure: Medium ($memory_pressure% free)\"\n308\t        else\n309\t            print_warning \"Memory pressure: High ($memory_pressure% free)\"\n310\t            print_info \"💡 Consider closing some applications\"\n311\t        fi\n312\t    fi\n313\t}\n314\t\n315\t# =============================================================================\n316\t# CPU Information\n317\t# =============================================================================\n318\t\n319\tsystem_cpu() {\n320\t    print_header \"⚡ CPU Information\"\n321\t    echo \"\"\n322\t    \n323\t    # CPU $(print_command \"$load_avg\")\"\n349\t}\n350\t\n351\t# =============================================================================\n352\t# Disk Usage\n353\t# =============================================================================\n354\t\n355\tsystem_disk_usage() {\n356\t    local target_dir=\"${1:-$HOME}\"\n357\t    \n358\t    if [[ ! -d \"$target_dir\" ]]; then\n359\t        print_error \"Directory not found: $target_dir\"\n360\t        return 1\n361\t    fi\n362\t    \n363\t    print_header \"💿 Disk Usage: $target_dir\"\n364\t Makefile:11: 'VERSION := 2.1.0'.\",\n      \"recommendation\": \"Define version in exactly one place (e.g., a lib/version.sh or config/config.json) and have all other locations read from it. This means search is only as good as the manually curated keyword lists, and adding new commands requires updating the search function manually. There is no way to auto-generate search from command definitions.\",\n      \"evidence\": \"Every module: finder_search() at finder.sh:245-271, wifi_search() at wifi.sh:430-456, etc. All use the same pattern of hardcoded if-checks against fixed strings.\",\n      \"recommendation\": \"Define command metadata as associative arrays (name -> description) and iterate over them for search. This would also auto-generate help text.\"\n    }\n  ],\n  \"strengths\": [\n    \"Clean dispatcher pattern: bin/mac uses a route_command() function with GLOBAL_SHORTCUTS and CATEGORIES dicts that cleanly delegates to module _dispatch() functions. The three-tier routing (main -> route_command -> module_dispatch) is well-structured.\",\n    \"Consistent module contract: Every module follows the same pattern with dispatch, help, and search functions. The naming convention ({module}_{action}, {module}_dispatch, {module}_help) is uniform across all 9 modules.\",\n    \"Good defensive programming: set -euo pipefail in the main dispatcher, extensive argument validation in module functions, graceful fallbacks (e.g., wifi module falls back from airport to networksetup, audio module falls back from SwitchAudioSource to system_profiler).\",\n    \"Polished UX: Color output with terminal detection, box-drawing characters, consistent formatting, contextual tips on every command, progress bars, and help text with examples on every module.\",\n    \"On-demand module loading: Modules are only loaded when their category is invoked (lazy loading via load_module()), not at startup. This keeps initial invocation fast.\",\n    \"Well-structured Makefile: 330 lines with targets for setup, testing (per-module, quick, performance), linting, formatting, building, packaging, CI, and version management. The help target with auto-documentation is particularly clean.\",\n    \"No circular dependencies: The dependency graph is strictly tree-shaped (utils <- modules), with only one optional cross-module reference (network -> wifi).\"\n  ],\n  \"dependency_graph\": \"utils.sh (loaded first, always)\\n  |\\n  +-- finder.sh (independent)\\n  +-- wifi.sh (independent)\\n  +-- network.sh (optional: probes wifi_get_current_network at runtime)\\n  +-- system.sh (independent)\\n  +-- dev.sh (independent)\\n  +-- display.sh (independent)\\n  +-- dock.sh (independent)\\n  +-- audio.sh (independent)\\n  +-- screenshot.sh (independent)\\n\\nbin/mac (dispatcher)\\n  |\\n  +-- sources utils.sh at startup\\n  +-- loads modules on-demand via load_module()\\n  +-- resolves GLOBAL_SHORTCUTS to category:action pairs\\n\\nNo circular dependencies exist.\\nOnly one cross-module reference: network -> wifi (optional, via declare -f probe).\\nAll modules depend exclusively on utils.sh.\"\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## SuperMac Architecture Audit -- Detailed Analysis\n\n### 1. Project Overview\n\nSuperMac v2.1.0 is a modular Bash CLI for macOS system management. It uses a dispatcher pattern where `bin/mac` routes commands to lazy-loaded module files in `lib/`. The project has 9 functional modules covering Finder, WiFi, networking, system info/maintenance, developer tools, display settings, dock management, audio control, and screenshots, backed by a shared utilities library. Total codebase is approximately 4,800 lines of functional code (excluding duplicates).\n\n### 2. Dependency Graph and Module Coupling\n\n```\n                    bin/mac (dispatcher, 349L)\n                        |\n                    sources utils.sh\n                        |\n            +-----------+-----------+\n            |                       |\n        utils.sh (589L)      config.json (65L, unused)\n            |\n    +---+---+---+---+---+---+---+---+---+\n    |   |   |   |   |   |   |   |   |   |\n   find wifi net sys dev dsp dock aud ssc\n   313L 507 484 541 610 428 573 519 590\n\n   Cross-module:\n   network ---> wifi (optional, runtime probe)\n```\n\nThe dependency graph is essentially flat. Every module depends only on `utils.sh` and is otherwise independent. This is a strong architectural choice. The single cross-module dependency (network optionally calling wifi functions via `declare -f` probing at `network.sh:180`) is handled gracefully with a fallback path. There are no circular dependencies.\n\n**Coupling score: 75/100** -- Loose coupling is achieved. The only concern is that utils.sh acts as a shared god-file, meaning any change to it potentially affects all modules. The `export -f` block at `utils.sh:575-587` exports 47 functions into the global namespace, which is a form of implicit coupling.\n\n### 3. Separation of Concerns\n\nEach module generally owns one macOS domain:\n\n| Module | Domain | Lines | Verdict |\n|--------|--------|-------|---------|\n| finder | File visibility & Finder | 313 | Clean |\n| wifi | WiFi connectivity | 507 | Clean |\n| network | IP, DNS, network diag | 484 | Mostly clean |\n| system | System info & maintenance | 541 | Cleanup scope too broad |\n| dev | Dev tools & encoding | 610 | Two unrelated domains |\n| display | Brightness & appearance | 428 | Clean |\n| dock | Dock positioning & config | 573 | Clean |\n| audio | Volume & device switching | 519 | Clean |\n| screenshot | Screenshot settings | 590 | Clean |\n\nThe dev module is the worst offender. Lines 30-315 handle process and server management (kill-port, list-ports, servers, localhost, serve, processes, cpu-hogs, memory-hogs). Lines 321-461 handle encoding and generation (json-format, base64-encode, base64-decode, uuid, password). These are two completely unrelated domains crammed into one module because both appeal to \"developers.\" The process management commands overlap significantly with the system module's `system_processes()` function, which does nearly the same thing (`system.sh:388-413` vs `dev.sh:230-271`).\n\nThe system module's `system_cleanup()` function at lines 109-185 also conflates too many concerns: it handles cache cleanup, download pruning, trash emptying, system log rotation, Safari cache clearing, temp file removal, and font cache clearing in a single function with a single confirmation prompt. The `rm -rf /tmp/*` at line 173 is particularly concerning.\n\n**Separation score: 70/100** -- Generally good domain boundaries, but dev module has a split personality and system cleanup needs tighter scoping.\n\n### 4. Extensibility Analysis\n\nAdding a new module requires touching at least 3 files manually:\n\n1. Create `lib/newmod.sh` with the required pattern (dispatch, help, search, action functions)\n2. Add entry to `CATEGORIES` dict in `bin/mac` at line 47\n3. Add to test module lists in `tests/test.sh` at lines 81, 131, 160, 196\n\nOptionally:\n4. Add global shortcuts to `GLOBAL_SHORTCUTS` in `bin/mac` at line 60\n5. Add aliases to `config.json`\n6. Add category entry to `config.json`\n\nThere is no auto-discovery mechanism. The `get_available_modules()` function at `utils.sh:524-529` is capable of scanning `lib/*.sh`, but it is never called by the dispatcher. The dispatcher relies entirely on the hardcoded `CATEGORIES` associative array.\n\nThere is no module template file, no scaffolding script, no `mac create-module` command. A new contributor would need to read an existing module and manually replicate the pattern.\n\nThe module contract itself is well-defined and consistent:\n- `{name}_dispatch(action, args...)` -- routes actions to handler functions\n- `{name}_help()` -- prints formatted help\n- `{name}_search(term)` -- returns matching commands\n- `{name}_{action}(args...)` -- individual action handlers\n\nThis contract could easily be formalized and auto-validated.\n\n**Extensibility score: 55/100** -- The contract is clean but the registration process is manual and error-prone. No template, no auto-discovery, no scaffolding.\n\n### 5. Shared Utilities (utils.sh) Assessment\n\n`utils.sh` at 589 lines is a catch-all utility file containing:\n\n| Section | Lines | Functions | Could Extract |\n|---------|-------|-----------|---------------|\n| Constants/Colors | 23-83 | N/A (readonly vars) | Yes -> colors.sh |\n| Output functions | 88-206 | 15 print_* functions | Yes -> output.sh |\n| Validation | 212-248 | 5 check/is functions | Yes -> validation.sh |\n| System info | 254-277 | 5 get_* functions | Yes -> sysinfo.sh |\n| User interaction | 284-347 | 2 functions (confirm, prompt_input) | Yes -> interaction.sh |\n| String ops | 353-378 | 4 functions | Yes -> strings.sh |\n| Array ops | 384-411 | 2 functions | Yes -> arrays.sh |\n| Config/Module/Debug/Error | 415-589 | ~12 functions | Core infrastructure |\n\nThe file serves as both a \"standard library\" and a \"runtime infrastructure\" module. The color constants alone take 60 lines. The box-drawing characters take 20 lines. These are never going to change and add noise to the file.\n\nOn the positive side:\n- The `load_module()` function provides clean lazy-loading\n- The `get_config()` function provides a config abstraction (even if unused)\n- Error handling with `die()` and `cleanup()` is properly structured\n- The `print_*` function hierarchy (success/error/info/warning/debug) is well-designed\n\nThe `export -f` block at lines 575-587 exports 47 functions. This is heavy but necessary in Bash since subshells created by pipes and command substitution do not inherit functions.\n\n**Shared utilities score: 65/100** -- Functional but bloated. The single-file approach makes it hard to navigate and modify. The config reading infrastructure exists but is completely unused by modules.\n\n### 6. File Organization Assessment\n\nThis is the weakest aspect of the project. The file tree has severe duplication:\n\n```\nSuperMac/\n  bin/mac          <-- canonical dispatcher\n  lib/*.sh (10)    <-- canonical modules\n  config/config.json <-- canonical config\n  tests/test.sh    <-- canonical tests\n\n  mac              <-- duplicate of bin/mac\n  *.sh (13)        <-- duplicates of lib/*.sh + install + setup + test\n  config.json      <-- duplicate of config/config.json\n```\n\nEvery file is confirmed identical via diff. The root directory contains 14 duplicated files totaling approximately 200KB. This creates confusion about which file is authoritative, bloats git history, and makes it unclear where to make edits. A contributor might edit `finder.sh` at the root and not realize the running code uses `lib/finder.sh`.\n\nAdditionally:\n- `install.sh` at the root (356 lines) is not in `bin/` -- inconsistent\n- `setup.sh` at the root (436 lines) is not in `bin/` -- inconsistent\n- `test.sh` at the root (509 lines) duplicates `tests/test.sh` -- wait, it does not. Let me verify.\n\nThe `tests/` directory contains `test.sh`, and there is also a root `test.sh`. The root `install.sh` and `setup.sh` have no counterparts in `bin/` (the bin/ only contains `mac` and `install.sh`). This inconsistency means the file organization story is incomplete even for non-duplicated files.\n\n**File organization score: 35/100** -- The canonical structure (bin/, lib/, config/, tests/) is well-conceived but completely undermined by identical root-level copies. This is the most critical organizational issue.\n\n### 7. Configuration Architecture\n\nThe `config.json` file at 65 lines defines:\n- `version`: \"2.1.0\"\n- `command_name`: \"mac\"\n- `default_settings`: screenshot_location, screenshot_format, volume_step, brightness_step, color_output, debug_mode, auto_update_check\n- `aliases`: ip, cleanup, restart-finder, kp, vol, dark, light\n- `categories`: 9 entries with enabled flags and descriptions\n- `user_preferences`: favorite_commands, command_history, last_used\n\nThe configuration system has a critical implementation gap:\n\n**What config.json declares vs. what the code actually uses:**\n\n| Config field | Declared | Consumed at runtime |\n|-------------|----------|-------------------|\n| default_settings.screenshot_location | Yes | No -- screenshot module hardcodes Desktop |\n| default_settings.screenshot_format | Yes | No -- screenshot module reads from defaults |\n| default_settings.volume_step | Yes | No -- audio module hardcodes step of 10 |\n| default_settings.brightness_step | Yes | No -- display module has no step concept |\n| default_settings.color_output | Yes | No -- colors are determined by terminal check |\n| default_settings.debug_mode | Yes | No -- debug is set via CLI flag |\n| default_settings.auto_update_check | Yes | No -- no update mechanism exists |\n| aliases | Yes | No -- hardcoded in bin/mac GLOBAL_SHORTCUTS |\n| categories.*.enabled | Yes | No -- all categories are always enabled |\n| user_preferences | Yes | No -- never read or written |\n\nThe `get_config()` function at `utils.sh:429-441` is the sole bridge between config.json and the code, but zero modules call it. The configuration file is effectively documentation that the code ignores.\n\n**Configuration score: 50/100** -- The schema is well-designed, but it is completely disconnected from the runtime. The config file is decorative.\n\n### 8. Plugin/Extension System\n\nThere is no plugin architecture. The `plugins/` directory exists but contains only a symlink to an external project (`ClaudeCodeSetup/plugins/internal`) and an 85-byte `registry.json` -- these appear to be artifacts from a different tool, not related to SuperMac's module system.\n\nThird-party extensions would currently require:\n1. Creating a new `.sh` file in `lib/`\n2. Manually editing `bin/mac` to add the category\n3. Manually editing `config.json` to add the category entry\n4. Manually editing `tests/test.sh` to add test coverage\n\nThere is no way to \"drop in\" a module without modifying core files.\n\n### 9. Scalability Assessment\n\nThe current architecture will face specific challenges as it grows:\n\n**Startup latency**: Currently, only `utils.sh` is loaded at startup (~589 lines sourced). Modules load on demand. This is good and will scale well to 20+ modules since only the invoked module is sourced.\n\n**Command routing**: The dispatcher uses a flat case statement in each module's `_dispatch()` function. As action count grows per module, these case statements will become unwieldy. The dev module already has 13 actions in its dispatcher.\n\n**Namespace pollution**: Every module sources into the global namespace. The finder module alone defines 11 functions, and dev defines 18. With 20 modules, there would be 200+ global functions. The `export -f` block already exports 47 functions. Bash has no module scoping, so collisions become likely.\n\n**Test scalability**: The test suite hardcodes module lists in 4 separate locations. Adding a module means updating all 4. There is no test discovery mechanism.\n\n**Search scalability**: Each module's search function uses hardcoded substring matching against fixed keywords. This does not scale to large command sets and produces inconsistent results.\n\n**Configuration scalability**: The config.json is read via `jq` for each `get_config()` call. If modules start using it heavily, this becomes a performance bottleneck (spawning a jq process per config read).\n\n### 10. Architecture Diagrams\n\n**Current execution flow:**\n```\nUser: mac wifi status\n         |\n         v\n    bin/mac main()\n         |\n         v\n    validate_environment()  -- check macOS, check lib/ dir\n         |\n         v\n    route_command(\"wifi\", \"status\")\n         |\n         +--> check GLOBAL_SHORTCUTS[\"wifi\"]  -- not found\n         |\n         +--> check CATEGORIES[\"wifi\"]        -- found\n         |\n         v\n    load_module(\"wifi\")     -- source lib/wifi.sh\n         |\n         v\n    wifi_dispatch(\"status\") -- case -> wifi_status()\n         |\n         v\n    wifi_status()           -- calls wifi_get_interface(),\n                             --   wifi_get_power_state(),\n                             --   wifi_show_current_connection()\n                             -- all from wifi module + utils.sh\n```\n\n**Current dependency map (actual runtime):**\n```\n[bin/mac] ---> [utils.sh] ---> macOS system commands\n     |              |\n     |              +-- osascript, defaults, system_profiler\n     |              +-- sw_vers, uname, networksetup\n     |\n     +--(on demand)--> [lib/finder.sh] ---> utils.sh only\n     +--(on demand)--> [lib/wifi.sh]  ---> utils.sh only\n     +--(on demand)--> [lib/network.sh] --> utils.sh + (optional) wifi.sh\n     +--(on demand)--> [lib/system.sh] ---> utils.sh only\n     +--(on demand)--> [lib/dev.sh]  ---> utils.sh only\n     +--(on demand)--> [lib/display.sh] -> utils.sh only\n     +--(on demand)--> [lib/dock.sh]  ---> utils.sh only\n     +--(on demand)--> [lib/audio.sh] --> utils.sh only\n     +--(on demand)--> [lib/screenshot.sh] -> utils.sh only\n```\n\n**Proposed improved architecture:**\n```\n[bin/mac]\n     |\n     v\n[lib/bootstrap.sh] --- single entry, sources all libs\n     |\n     +-- [lib/colors.sh]     -- terminal color constants\n     +-- [lib/output.sh]     -- print_*, banner, box, progress\n     +-- [lib/validation.sh] -- check_macos, is_number, is_in_range\n     +-- [lib/interaction.sh] -- confirm, prompt_input\n     +-- [lib/strings.sh]    -- to_lower, trim, pad\n     +-- [lib/config.sh]     -- config reading + writing\n     +-- [lib/loader.sh]     -- module loading, discovery, validation\n     |\n     +--(on demand)--> [lib/modules/*.sh]  -- auto-discovered\n     |                    each declares: _meta, _dispatch, _help, _search\n     |\n     +-- [config/config.json] -- consumed by lib/config.sh\n```\n\n### 11. Concrete Improvement Recommendations\n\n**Priority 1 -- File cleanup (CRITICAL):**\nDelete all 14 duplicate files at the project root. This is a zero-risk change that eliminates confusion. Add a `.gitignore` entry or a Makefile check to prevent future root-level .sh file accumulation.\n\n**Priority 2 -- Make config.json functional (HIGH):**\nEither connect `get_config()` to actual module behavior or remove the unused fields. A pragmatic approach: have each module read its defaults from config on first call (e.g., `screenshot_get_format()` checks config.json before falling back to `defaults read`). Add a `mac config` command to view/edit settings.\n\n**Priority 3 -- Module auto-discovery (HIGH):**\nReplace the hardcoded `CATEGORIES` dict with runtime discovery. Each module defines a `{name}_meta()` function that outputs `name:emoji:description`. The dispatcher scans `lib/*.sh`, sources each to call `_meta()`, and builds the category registry dynamically. This eliminates the need to edit `bin/mac` when adding modules.\n\n**Priority 4 -- Split utils.sh (MEDIUM):**\nExtract the 8 logical sections of utils.sh into focused files under `lib/`. The dispatcher sources a small bootstrap file that loads them all. Modules continue to call the same functions; only the file organization changes.\n\n**Priority 5 -- Split dev module (MEDIUM):**\nMove encoding/utility functions (base64, uuid, password, json-format) to a new `lib/tools.sh` module. Keep `lib/dev.sh` focused on developer workflow (ports, servers, processes).\n\n**Priority 6 -- Version unification (LOW):**\nDefine `SUPERMAC_VERSION` in exactly one location. The best candidate is `config/config.json` since it is the single source of truth for metadata. Have utils.sh read it from there, and have the Makefile pull it from config.json.\n\n**Priority 7 -- Fix test coverage gaps (LOW):**\nAdd dock, audio, and screenshot to all module lists in `tests/test.sh`. Add functional test cases for each (at minimum: status commands, help commands, error handling).\n\n### 12. Summary Scores\n\n| Category | Score | Rationale |\n|----------|-------|-----------|\n| Module Coupling | 75/100 | Flat dependency tree, one optional cross-module ref. Loses points for utils.sh as god-file. |\n| Separation of Concerns | 70/100 | Clean domain boundaries for 7 of 9 modules. Dev module conflates unrelated concerns. System cleanup is over-broad. |\n| Extensibility | 55/100 | Consistent contract but manual registration, no auto-discovery, no template, no scaffolding. |\n| Shared Utilities | 65/100 | Well-designed function hierarchy but single 589-line file with 8 distinct responsibilities. |\n| File Organization | 35/100 | Canonical structure is correct but completely undermined by 14 identical root-level duplicates. |\n| Configuration Design | 50/100 | Well-designed schema but zero runtime consumption. Config is decorative. |\n| **Overall** | **62/100** | Solid foundation with clean patterns, undermined by file duplication, unused config, and no auto-discovery. |\n\nThe architecture's bones are good. The dispatcher pattern, lazy module loading, consistent module contract, and loose coupling are all sound design decisions. The main issues are housekeeping (duplicate files), incomplete implementation (unused config system), and missing infrastructure (auto-discovery, module templates). These are all fixable without breaking the existing module contract."}],"stop_reason":"end_turn","stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":274,"cache_creation_input_tokens":0,"cache_read_input_tokens":77184,"output_tokens":7538,"server_tool_use":{"web_search_requests":0,"web_fetch_requests":0},"service_tier":"standard","cache_creation":{"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0},"inference_geo":"","iterations":[],"speed":"standard"}},"type":"assistant","uuid":"8640860c-cae5-4558-bd6b-3dae57e9863d","timestamp":"2026-04-07T13:19:11.698Z","userType":"external","entrypoint":"cli","cwd":"/Users/gab/PROJECTS/SuperMac","sessionId":"ee896f3b-ba3e-493e-ab51-73d0ef866e89","version":"2.1.92","gitBranch":"main","slug":"binary-sauteeing-dragonfly"}
